## Section 001: Rust Backend Reference Routing
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed theme name says routing but the seed never explains what is routed, the 83-line mapped map is a dispatcher that turns an incoming backend task into a work mode and an ordered list of which bundle files to read next
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the map exists because the bundle is too large to read whole per task, its opening line says to use it first to route the request before loading heavier backend references, making cheap routing the guard on expensive reading
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: skipping the router and opening bundle files by filename intuition reproduces the misreads the map prevents, migration sequencing hunted in the playbook, session flows hunted in testing files
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this reference covers dispatch into the rust-web-backend-delivery bundle, the content of the destination files is each destination's own subject
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to frame this document as the corpus mirror of the bundle's dispatcher, its unit of value is a correct file-and-section read order, not backend advice of its own
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the map is deliberately the only file with no backend content at all, every one of its 83 lines is either a routing condition or a destination, which is what lets it stay cheap enough to consult on every task
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Reference Routing", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to consult the map before opening any other bundle file and follow the read order it emits for the classified mode or task type
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Reference Routing", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the map exists because the bundle is too large to read whole per task, its opening line says to use it first to route the request before loading heavier backend references, making cheap routing the guard on expensive reading
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Reference Routing", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; skipping the router and opening bundle files by filename intuition reproduces the misreads the map prevents, migration sequencing hunted in the playbook, session flows hunted in testing files
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Reference Routing", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this reference covers dispatch into the rust-web-backend-delivery bundle, the content of the destination files is each destination's own subject
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Reference Routing", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: frame this document as the corpus mirror of the bundle's dispatcher, its unit of value is a correct file-and-section read order, not backend advice of its own
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Reference Routing", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the map is deliberately the only file with no backend content at all, every one of its 83 lines is either a routing condition or a destination, which is what lets it stay cheap enough to consult on every task

## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed table's local row maps only reference-map.md, the router, while every destination the router points at, the playbook and three risk files, sits outside the mapped set even though routing claims are meaningless without their targets
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a router's correctness is defined by its destinations, so this theme's evidence base necessarily spans the whole bundle, and destination facts used here must be cited to their own files by name rather than to the mapped router row
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: attributing a destination's content to the router row, for example quoting harness rules as if the map contained them, blurs the exact boundary this table exists to keep
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the table certifies where this document's claims come from, it does not certify the four external URLs, which stayed unretrieved throughout this evolution
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to hold the router as the anchor row and cite each destination file explicitly whenever its content, not its address, is used
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that of the corpus's two rust-web-backend themes, the playbook theme anchors the content chapter and this theme anchors the dispatcher, together the two mapped rows cover the bundle's control plane and its largest data plane

- **supporting_reason:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the mode table is built on risk ownership, each mode row names a main-risk condition, ambiguity, delivery sequencing, operational safety, security, resilience, or review readiness, and maps it to the files that own that risk class
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: risk-blind routing reads by topic keyword instead, a retries question matches resilience risk and belongs in security-and-resilience, but keyword routing sends it to the playbook because retry appears in the client-boundary section

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed four bullets tell an agent to start with the source map but not how to route, the operative procedure is the map's own, classify mode or task type, emit the file list in prescribed order, read only that list, then act
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because agents suffer routing failures worse than humans, an agent that loads the full bundle spends context on files its task never needed, and one that keyword-routes confidently misreads never notices, so mechanical adherence to the map is the cheapest reliability lever available
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: an agent prompt that says use the rust backend bundle without the routing step produces exactly the fallback-abuse and keyword-routing defects the registry names, at machine speed
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this guide scripts agent dispatch into the bundle, what the agent does inside each destination follows that destination's own guidance
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to give agents the literal three-step routine, classify, emit ordered file list with the governing map row cited, read and act, logging all three steps
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the map's structure is machine-friendly by accident, its tables map conditions to file lists, so an agent can be required to quote the exact row it matched, making every routing decision verifiable from the log alone

## Section 013: Theme Specific Artifact
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed named artifact, canonical routing rules for stale, duplicate, and conflicting sources, has no concrete form in the seed, its natural shape is a per-team routing card, one page mapping local task vocabulary onto the map's rows
- **supporting_reason:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because teams phrase tasks in product words, fix checkout emails, while the map speaks in risk words, external integration with resilience concerns, the routing card is the translation layer that makes the map's rows reachable from the words tickets actually use
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: without the translation layer each engineer improvises the product-to-risk mapping, and improvised mappings are where keyword routing re-enters through the back door
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the card translates into the map, it must never bypass it, a card row points at a map row, not directly at files
- **revision_decision:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to define the artifact as the routing card, ticket-vocabulary phrases on the left, matched map rows on the right, reviewed whenever the map or the product vocabulary shifts
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that pointing card rows at map rows rather than files makes the card revision-proof, when a bundle update changes a row's file list, every card entry inherits the fix without editing, the indirection is the maintenance strategy

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed endpoint-count budget models destination work, not dispatch, routing's own workload unit is the classification event, seconds per task, plus the rarer card and map maintenance events measured in minutes per quarter
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because dispatch cost is deliberately front-loaded and tiny, the router's design pushes all heavy cost into the destinations it selects, so this theme's capacity question is not how much routing a team can afford but whether the near-zero cost stays near zero as task volume grows
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the model breaks when classification stops being cheap, ambiguous multi-risk tasks that take real deliberation to route signal either a task that should be split or a map row whose conditions have drifted from the work the team actually gets
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this model budgets dispatch effort, the selected destinations' implementation effort is budgeted by the playbook theme's slice model
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to restate the workload as classification events at seconds each, card maintenance at one page per quarter, and map-consistency checks per bundle revision
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that expensive routing is diagnostic, when a task resists the minute-scale lookup the resistance itself is information, the task is compound and should be split into slices that each route cleanly, dispatch difficulty predicting decomposition need
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to budget routing at under a minute per task, and treat any task exceeding that as a decomposition candidate before forcing a route
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because dispatch cost is deliberately front-loaded and tiny, the router's design pushes all heavy cost into the destinations it selects, so this theme's capacity question is not how much routing a team can afford but whether the near-zero cost stays near zero as task volume grows
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; the model breaks when classification stops being cheap, ambiguous multi-risk tasks that take real deliberation to route signal either a task that should be split or a map row whose conditions have drifted from the work the team actually gets
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this model budgets dispatch effort, the selected destinations' implementation effort is budgeted by the playbook theme's slice model
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: restate the workload as classification events at seconds each, card maintenance at one page per quarter, and map-consistency checks per bundle revision
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies expensive routing is diagnostic, when a task resists the minute-scale lookup the resistance itself is information, the task is compound and should be split into slices that each route cleanly, dispatch difficulty predicting decomposition need
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: tasks arrive at slice granularity, portfolio-level initiatives route per constituent slice, not once at the top
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because dispatch cost is deliberately front-loaded and tiny, the router's design pushes all heavy cost into the destinations it selects, so this theme's capacity question is not how much routing a team can afford but whether the near-zero cost stays near zero as task volume grows

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: the model breaks when classification stops being cheap, ambiguous multi-risk tasks that take real deliberation to route signal either a task that should be split or a map row whose conditions have drifted from the work the team actually gets
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are batching routing across many tickets to save seconds recreates standing-habit drift, the per-task cost being trivial is exactly why it should be paid per task

## Section 020: Failure Mode Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed seed's drift and surge rows miss the router's specific decay modes, coupling rot where destination revisions stale the map's inline section names, vocabulary drift where new ticket language stops matching row conditions, and revision lag where the bundle updates and routed habits do not
- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because all three are synchronization failures between artifacts on different change cadences, destinations change faster than the router, product vocabulary changes faster than the card, and the bundle changes faster than memorized habits
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: each mode fails softly, routes keep resolving to plausible files while their precision quietly degrades, the reader gets a working-looking dispatch whose section-level accuracy is gone
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this table catalogs dispatch decay, decay of the destination content itself belongs to the playbook theme's failure table
- **revision_decision:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the three synchronization rows, coupling rot caught by the heading-consistency script, vocabulary drift caught by card review against fresh tickets, revision lag caught by re-announcing routes after bundle changes
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the three modes share one mitigation shape, re-synchronization triggered by the faster artifact's change events, which means none needs a calendar, each needs a hook on the event that causes it, revision hooks beating scheduled reviews for all three

- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to wire each detection to its triggering event, bundle change runs the script, quarterly ticket sample refreshes the card, and archive updates invalidate memorized routes explicitly

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed seed's retry bullets govern corpus generation, while dispatch has its own retry question, what to do when a route fails, the files read did not answer the task, and naive re-routing just re-runs the same lookup into the same miss
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a failed route means the classification was wrong or the map lacks a row, so the retry ladder is diagnostic, first re-classify with the task's surprise information, then escalate a tier toward the fallback sequence, then treat the miss as a map gap and route by nearest row while recording the gap
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the anti-pattern is silent looping, re-reading the same prescribed files hoping for a different answer, or abandoning routing entirely after one miss and reverting to keyword habits
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this section governs retrying dispatch decisions, retrying backend operations at runtime is destination content owned by the security sibling and routed accordingly
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the dispatch retry ladder, one re-classification with new information, one tier escalation, then a recorded map-gap workaround, with backpressure halting new routing shortcuts while known gaps sit unrecorded
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that route misses are the map's only organic improvement signal, a recorded gap with the workaround chosen is a draft row for the next map revision, so the retry ladder's final step is simultaneously failure handling and the map's evolution mechanism

- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to allow two structured retries per failed route, re-classify then escalate, and convert any third miss into a recorded gap rather than another attempt
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because a failed route means the classification was wrong or the map lacks a row, so the retry ladder is diagnostic, first re-classify with the task's surprise information, then escalate a tier toward the fallback sequence, then treat the miss as a map gap and route by nearest row while recording the gap

- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add the dispatch retry ladder, one re-classification with new information, one tier escalation, then a recorded map-gap workaround, with backpressure halting new routing shortcuts while known gaps sit unrecorded

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed seed logs latency and error counters, but dispatch observability needs different records, the route declaration per task, the map row cited, deviations with reasons, mid-task re-routes, and recorded route misses with their workarounds
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because every routing metric, target, and failure detector defined above consumes these records, without them the declaration rate, match rate, tier attributions, and map-gap signals are all unmeasurable, the checklist is the data layer under the whole practice
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: routing that leaves no trace makes every later audit reconstruct from memory, and memory reconstructs the route that should have happened, not the one that did
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this checklist specifies dispatch records, service runtime observability is destination content that routes to the ops sibling
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to define the minimal route record, task identifier, cited map row, file list emitted, deviations with reasons, re-routes, and misses, one or two lines per task in the existing review flow
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the route record is self-describing in a way code telemetry is not, citing the map row embeds the expected file list by reference, so a single line captures both what was prescribed and what was done, the comparison any audit needs
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to emit the route record at review time in the PR description or review template, keeping it terse enough that emission survives deadline pressure
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because every routing metric, target, and failure detector defined above consumes these records, without them the declaration rate, match rate, tier attributions, and map-gap signals are all unmeasurable, the checklist is the data layer under the whole practice
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; routing that leaves no trace makes every later audit reconstruct from memory, and memory reconstructs the route that should have happened, not the one that did
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this checklist specifies dispatch records, service runtime observability is destination content that routes to the ops sibling
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: define the minimal route record, task identifier, cited map row, file list emitted, deviations with reasons, re-routes, and misses, one or two lines per task in the existing review flow
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the route record is self-describing in a way code telemetry is not, citing the map row embeds the expected file list by reference, so a single line captures both what was prescribed and what was done, the comparison any audit needs

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed latency ceilings measure services, but this theme's performance question is dispatch speed and precision, how quickly a task resolves to its file list and how little excess reading the list contains
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because routing performance has two axes that trade against each other, faster routes come from coarser tiers which prescribe more reading, so the verification method must measure both lookup time and read-list precision, not either alone
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: optimizing lookup speed alone drives everyone to the fallback sequence, instant to choose and maximally wasteful to execute, the seed's own pass condition, identifying the next action without reading unrelated files, is precisely the precision axis
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this method verifies dispatch performance, the routed destinations' runtime performance methods are their own subject
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to measure per-route lookup time against the minute budget and read-list precision as the share of prescribed files that proved relevant, reviewing both distributions quarterly
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that precision is measurable retroactively from route records plus outcomes, a prescribed file whose content shaped no decision was excess, so the same records powering match-rate audits also price each tier's real reading cost, no new instrumentation needed

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed seed bounds task scale, but routing has its own scale seams, the map serves one bundle, so more bundles need a router of routers, more teams multiply vocabulary cards, and heavier task volume eventually demands routing automation
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because each seam follows from a linear assumption in the current design, one map assumes one destination set, one card assumes one team vocabulary, and manual lookup assumes task volume where seconds-scale routing stays negligible in aggregate
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: stretching past the seams without redesign produces predictable shapes, cross-bundle questions bouncing between corpus themes with no dispatcher above them, and card forks drifting apart across teams until the same ticket routes differently by floor
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this statement bounds the dispatch practice, the destination content's scale limits are stated by the playbook theme's boundary section
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to name the three seams, corpus-level routing needs its own layer above per-bundle maps, multi-team use needs card governance, and volume growth needs the route record automated before the manual practice collapses
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that this corpus is already pressing the first seam, its adjacent-routing sections are a distributed router of routers, each theme pointing sideways at its neighbors, the seam is crossed not by one new artifact but by keeping those distributed pointers mutually consistent
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to run the practice as designed within one bundle, one team, and human-speed volume, and treat any seam crossing as a design event for the routing layer itself
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because each seam follows from a linear assumption in the current design, one map assumes one destination set, one card assumes one team vocabulary, and manual lookup assumes task volume where seconds-scale routing stays negligible in aggregate
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; stretching past the seams without redesign produces predictable shapes, cross-bundle questions bouncing between corpus themes with no dispatcher above them, and card forks drifting apart across teams until the same ticket routes differently by floor
